id="cite_ref-e_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-e-17">[f]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Spain</b> (Spanish: <i lang="es">España</i>, <small></small><span class="IPA" lang="es-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[esˈpaɲa]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Es-Espa%C3%B1a.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/64/Es-Espa%C3%B1a.ogg" title="Es-España.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>), or the <b>Kingdom of Spain</b> (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Reino de España</i></span>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nation_name_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-nation_name-18">[g]</a></sup> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcontinental_country" title="Transcontinental country">transcontinental country</a> predominantly located in southwestern <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> with parts of territory in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> and across the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-19">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[h]</a></sup> The largest part of Spain is situated on the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>; its territory also includes the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> in the Atlantic Ocean, the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a> in the Mediterranean Sea, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_cities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous cities of Spain">autonomous cities</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a> in Africa. The country's mainland is bordered to the south by <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>; to the south and east by the Mediterranean Sea; to the north by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Bay of Biscay</a>; and to the west by <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and the Atlantic Ocean. With an area of 505,990 km<sup>2</sup> (195,360 sq mi), Spain is the second-largest country in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) and, with a population exceeding 47.4 million, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_European_Union_countries" title="List of European Union countries">fourth-most populous</a> EU member state. Spain's capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>; other major <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Spain" title="List of metropolitan areas in Spain">urban areas</a> include <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zaragoza" title="Zaragoza">Zaragoza</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="Málaga">Málaga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murcia" title="Murcia">Murcia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca" title="Palma de Mallorca">Palma de Mallorca</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_De_Gran_Canaria" title="Las Palmas De Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a>.
</p><p>Anatomically modern humans first arrived in the Iberian Peninsula around 42,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lillios2019_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lillios2019-21">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="List of the Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">Pre-Roman peoples</a> dwelled in the territory, in addition to the development of coastal trading colonies by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phoenicians" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greeks</a> and the brief <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carthaginians" title="Carthaginians">Carthaginian</a> rule over the Mediterranean coastline. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Hispania" title="Roman Hispania">Roman conquest and colonization of the peninsula (Hispania)</a> ensued, bringing a <a href="/wiki/Romanization_(cultural)" title="Romanization (cultural)">Roman acculturation</a> of the population. Hispania remained under Roman rule until <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">the collapse of the Western Roman Empire</a> in the fourth century, which ushered in the <a href="/wiki/Migration_Period" title="Migration Period">migration</a> of <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic peoples</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a>  into the peninsula. Eventually, the <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigoths</a> emerged as the dominant power in the peninsula by the fifth century. In the early eighth century, most of the peninsula was <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">conquered by the Umayyad Caliphate</a> and during early Islamic rule, <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Al-Andalus</a> became the dominant peninsular power, centered in <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" title="Córdoba, Spain">Córdoba</a>. Several Christian kingdoms emerged in Northern Iberia, chief among them <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Kingdom of León">León</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Castile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">Aragón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portugal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">Navarre</a> and over the next seven centuries, an intermittent southward expansion of these kingdoms, known as <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a>, culminated with the Christian seizure of the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Granada" title="Emirate of Granada">Emirate of Granada</a> in 1492. Jews and Muslims were forced to choose between conversion to Catholicism or expulsion and the <i><a href="/wiki/Morisco" title="Morisco">Morisco</a></i> converts were eventually <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Moriscos" title="Expulsion of the Moriscos">expelled</a>. The dynastic union of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a> was followed by the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Iberian_Navarre" title="Spanish conquest of Iberian Navarre">annexation of Navarre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">1580 incorporation of Portugal</a> (which ended in 1640). In the wake of the Spanish colonization of the Americas after 1492, the Crown came to hold <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">a large overseas empire</a>, which underpinned the emergence of a global trading system primarily fuelled by the precious metals extracted in the New World.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[14]</a></sup> Centralisation of the administration and further State-building in mainland Spain ensued in the 18th and 19th centuries, during which the Crown saw the loss of the bulk of its American colonies a few years after of the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a>. The country veered between different political regimes; monarchy and republic, and following a <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">1936–39 devastating civil war</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">fascist dictatorship</a> that lasted until 1975. With the restoration of Democracy under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">Spanish Constitution of 1978</a> and the entry into the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> in 1986, the country experienced profound social and political change as well as an important economic growth.
</p><p>Spanish <a href="/wiki/Spanish_art" title="Spanish art">art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Spain" title="Music of Spain">music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_literature" title="Spanish literature">literature</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_cuisine" title="Spanish cuisine">cuisine</a> have been influential worldwide, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>. As a reflection of its large <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Spain" title="Culture of Spain">cultural wealth</a>, Spain has the world's fourth-largest number of <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a> (49) and is the world's <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_rankings" title="World Tourism rankings">second-most visited country</a>. Its cultural influence extends over 570 million <a href="/wiki/Hispanophone" title="Hispanophone">Hispanophones</a>, making Spanish the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">second-most spoken native language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>Spain is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpanish_Constitution1978Article_1_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpanish_Constitution1978Article_1-24">[16]</a></sup> with King <a href="/wiki/Felipe_VI" title="Felipe VI">Felipe VI</a> as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>. It is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-income_country" title="High-income country">high-income country</a> and an advanced economy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[17]</a></sup> with the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">fourteenth-largest economy by nominal GDP</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">sixteenth-largest by PPP</a>. Spain has one of the longest <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancies</a> in the world at 83.5 years in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[18]</a></sup> It ranks particularly high in <a href="/wiki/Health_care_quality" title="Health care quality">healthcare quality</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PadrónMoreno2020_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-PadrónMoreno2020-27">[19]</a></sup> with its healthcare system considered to be one of the most efficient worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[20]</a></sup> It is a world leader in <a href="/wiki/Organ_transplantation" title="Organ transplantation">organ transplants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Organ_donation" title="Organ donation">organ donation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[22]</a></sup> Spain is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN), the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU), the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> (CoE), the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ibero-American_States" title="Organization of Ibero-American States">Organization of Ibero-American States</a> (OEI), the <a href="/wiki/Union_for_the_Mediterranean" title="Union for the Mediterranean">Union for the Mediterranean</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty_Organization" title="North Atlantic Treaty Organization">North Atlantic Treaty Organization</a> (NATO), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> (OECD), <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE), the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO) and many other international organisations.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<p>The origins of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> name <i><a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a></i>, and the modern <i>España</i>, are uncertain, although the Phoenicians and Carthaginians referred to the region as <i>Spania</i>, therefore the most widely accepted etymology is a <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>-<a href="/wiki/Phoenician_language" title="Phoenician language">Phoenician</a> one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[23]</a></sup> There have been a number of accounts and hypotheses of its origin:
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Lady_of_Elche,_once_polychrome_stone_bust_discovered_by_chance_in_1897_at_L%27Alc%C3%BAdia,_believed_to_be_a_piece_of_Iberian_sculpture_from_the_4th_century_BC,_National_Archaeological_Museum_of_Spain,_Madrid_(20098349590).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3955" data-file-width="3178" decoding="async" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/The_Lady_of_Elche%2C_once_polychrome_stone_bust_discovered_by_chance_in_1897_at_L%27Alc%C3%BAdia%2C_believed_to_be_a_piece_of_Iberian_sculpture_from_the_4th_century_BC%2C_National_Archaeological_Museum_of_Spain%2C_Madrid_%2820098349590%29.jpg/170px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/The_Lady_of_Elche%2C_once_polychrome_stone_bust_discovered_by_chance_in_1897_at_L%27Alc%C3%BAdia%2C_believed_to_be_a_piece_of_Iberian_sculpture_from_the_4th_century_BC%2C_National_Archaeological_Museum_of_Spain%2C_Madrid_%2820098349590%29.jpg/255px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/The_Lady_of_Elche%2C_once_polychrome_stone_bust_discovered_by_chance_in_1897_at_L%27Alc%C3%BAdia%2C_believed_to_be_a_piece_of_Iberian_sculpture_from_the_4th_century_BC%2C_National_Archaeological_Museum_of_Spain%2C_Madrid_%2820098349590%29.jpg/340px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Lady_of_Elche,_once_polychrome_stone_bust_discovered_by_chance_in_1897_at_L%27Alc%C3%BAdia,_believed_to_be_a_piece_of_Iberian_sculpture_from_the_4th_century_BC,_National_Archaeological_Museum_of_Spain,_Madrid_(20098349590).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Lady_of_Elche" title="Lady of Elche">Lady of Elche</a>, possibly depicting <a href="/wiki/Tanit" title="Tanit">Tanit</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Carthaginian_Iberia" title="Carthaginian Iberia">Carthaginian Iberia</a>, 4th century BCE</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> scholar <a href="/wiki/Antonio_de_Nebrija" title="Antonio de Nebrija">Antonio de Nebrija</a> proposed that the word <i>Hispania</i> evolved from the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_language" title="Iberian language">Iberian</a> word <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispalis" title="Hispalis">Hispalis</a></i>, meaning "city of the western world".
</p><p><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jes%C3%BAs_Luis_Cunchillos&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jesús Luis Cunchillos (page does not exist)">Jesús Luis Cunchillos</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jes%C3%BAs_Luis_Cunchillos" title="es:Jesús Luis Cunchillos">es</a>]</span> argued that the root of the term <i>span</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Phoenician_language" title="Phoenician language">Phoenician</a> word <i>spy</i>, meaning "to forge metals". Therefore, <i>i-spn-ya</i> would mean "the land where metals are forged".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[24]</a></sup> It may be a derivation of the Phoenician <i>I-Shpania</i>, meaning "island of rabbits", "land of rabbits" or "edge", a reference to Spain's location at the end of the Mediterranean; Roman coins struck in the region from the reign of <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">Hadrian</a> show a female figure with a rabbit at her feet,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-burke_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-burke-33">[25]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a> called it the "land of the rabbits".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spain_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spain-34">[26]</a></sup> The word in question (compare modern Hebrew <i>Shafan</i>) actually means "<a href="/wiki/Hyrax" title="Hyrax">Hyrax</a>", possibly due to Phoenicians confusing the two animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Hispania</i> may derive from the poetic use of the term <i><a href="/wiki/Hesperia_(mythology)" title="Hesperia (mythology)">Hesperia</a></i>, reflecting the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> perception of Italy as a "western land" or "land of the setting sun" (<i>Hesperia</i>, <i>Ἑσπερία</i> in <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>) and Spain, being still further west, as <i>Hesperia ultima</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anthon_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-anthon-36">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is the claim that "Hispania" derives from the <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> word <i>Ezpanna</i> meaning "edge" or "border", another reference to the fact that the Iberian Peninsula constitutes the southwest corner of the European continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anthon_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-anthon-36">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>Two 15th-century Spanish Jewish scholars, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isaac_Abravanel" title="Isaac Abravanel">Don Isaac Abravanel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Solomon_ibn_Verga" title="Solomon ibn Verga">Solomon ibn Verga</a>, gave an explanation now considered folkloric. Both men wrote in two different published works that the first Jews to reach Spain were brought by ship by Phiros who was confederate with the king of Babylon when he laid siege to Jerusalem. Phiros was a <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Grecian</a> by birth, but who had been given a kingdom in Spain. Phiros became related by marriage to Espan, the nephew of king Heracles, who also ruled over a kingdom in Spain. Heracles later renounced his throne in preference for his native Greece, leaving his kingdom to his nephew, Espan, from whom the country of <i>España</i> (Spain) took its name. Based upon their testimonies, this eponym would have already been in use in Spain by c. 350 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[29]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Spain" title="History of Spain">History of Spain</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_and_pre-Roman_peoples">Prehistory and pre-Roman peoples</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Iberia" title="Prehistoric Iberia">Prehistoric Iberia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3483" data-file-width="5225" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg/220px-2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg/330px-2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg/440px-2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Celtic castro in Galicia</div></div></div>
<p>Archaeological research at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaeological_Site_of_Atapuerca" title="Archaeological Site of Atapuerca">Atapuerca</a> indicates the Iberian Peninsula was populated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hominid" title="Hominid">hominids</a> 1.2 million years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[30]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Atapuerca_Mountains" title="Atapuerca Mountains">Atapuerca</a> fossils have been found of the earliest known <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hominins" title="Hominins">hominins</a> in Europe, <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_antecessor" title="Homo antecessor">Homo antecessor</a></i>. Modern humans first arrived in Iberia, from the north on foot, about 35,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[31]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2016)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup> The best known artefacts of these prehistoric human settlements are the famous paintings in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Altamira_(cave)" title="Altamira (cave)">Altamira cave</a> of Cantabria in northern Iberia, which were created from 35,600 to 13,500 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Before_Common_Era" title="Before Common Era">BCE</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cro-Magnon" title="Cro-Magnon">Cro-Magnon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Science2012_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Science2012-40">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[33]</a></sup> Archaeological and genetic evidence suggests that the Iberian Peninsula acted as one of several major refugia from which northern Europe was repopulated following the end of the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_glaciation" title="Quaternary glaciation">last ice age</a>.
</p><p>The largest groups inhabiting the Iberian Peninsula before the Roman conquest were the <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberians</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a>. The Iberians inhabited the Mediterranean side of the peninsula, from the northeast to the southeast. The Celts inhabited much of the interior and Atlantic side of the peninsula, from the northwest to the southwest. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basque_people" title="Basque people">Basques</a> occupied the western area of the Pyrenees mountain range and adjacent areas, the Phoenician-influenced <a href="/wiki/Tartessos" title="Tartessos">Tartessians</a> culture flourished in the southwest and the <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">Lusitanians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vettones" title="Vettones">Vettones</a> occupied areas in the central west. Several cities were founded along the coast by <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicians</a>, and trading outposts and colonies were established by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_colonies" title="Greek colonies">Greeks</a> in the East. Eventually, Phoenician-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carthaginians" title="Carthaginians">Carthaginians</a> expanded inland towards the meseta; however, due to the bellicose inland tribes, the Carthaginians got settled in the coasts of the Iberian Peninsula.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Hispania_and_the_Visigothic_Kingdom">Roman Hispania and the Visigothic Kingdom</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigothic Kingdom</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teatro_de_M%C3%A9rida,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2017_18.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Teatro_de_M%C3%A9rida%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2017_18.jpg/220px-Teatro_de_M%C3%A9rida%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2017_18.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Teatro_de_M%C3%A9rida%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2017_18.jpg/330px-Teatro_de_M%C3%A9rida%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2017_18.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Teatro_de_M%C3%A9rida%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2017_18.jpg/440px-Teatro_de_M%C3%A9rida%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2017_18.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teatro_de_M%C3%A9rida,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2017_18.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Theatre_(M%C3%A9rida)" title="Roman Theatre (Mérida)">Roman Theatre</a> in <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9rida,_Spain" title="Mérida, Spain">Mérida</a></div></div></div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Second_Punic_War" title="Second Punic War">Second Punic War</a>, roughly between 210 and 205 BCE the expanding <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> captured Carthaginian trading colonies along the Mediterranean coast. Although it took the Romans nearly two centuries to complete the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_the_Iberian_peninsula" title="Roman conquest of the Iberian peninsula">conquest of the Iberian Peninsula</a>, they retained control of it for over six centuries. Roman rule was bound together by law, language, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_road" title="Roman road">Roman road</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hispania_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-hispania-42">[34]</a></sup>
</p><p>The cultures of the pre-Roman populations were gradually <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Hispania" title="Romanization of Hispania">Romanised</a> (Latinised) at different rates depending on what part of the peninsula they lived in, with local leaders being admitted into the Roman aristocratic class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[i]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-country_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-country-44">[35]</a></sup> Hispania served as a granary for the Roman market, and its harbours exported gold, <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olive_oil" title="Olive oil">olive oil</a>, and wine. Agricultural production increased with the introduction of irrigation projects, some of which remain in use. Emperors <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">Hadrian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trajan" title="Trajan">Trajan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_I" title="Theodosius I">Theodosius I</a>, and the philosopher <a href="/wiki/Seneca_the_Younger" title="Seneca the Younger">Seneca</a> were born in Hispania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[j]</a></sup> Christianity was introduced into Hispania in the 1st century CE and it became popular in the cities in the 2nd century CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-country_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-country-44">[35]</a></sup> Most of Spain's present languages and religion, and the basis of its laws, originate from this period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hispania_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-hispania-42">[34]</a></sup> In the late 2nd century (starting in 170 CE) incursions of North-African <a href="/wiki/Mauri" title="Mauri">Mauri</a> in the province of <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Baetica" title="Hispania Baetica">Baetica</a> took place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[36]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Concil_Toled.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="325" data-file-width="367" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Concil_Toled.jpg/220px-Concil_Toled.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Concil_Toled.jpg/330px-Concil_Toled.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Concil_Toled.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Concil_Toled.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Reccared_I" title="Reccared I">Reccared I</a> and bishops during <a href="/wiki/Councils_of_Toledo" title="Councils of Toledo">Council III of Toledo</a>, 589. <a href="/wiki/Codex_Vigilanus" title="Codex Vigilanus">Codex Vigilanus</a>, fol. 145, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Biblioteca_de_San_Lorenzo_de_El_Escorial" title="Real Biblioteca de San Lorenzo de El Escorial">Biblioteca del Escorial</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a>, together with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sarmatian" title="Sarmatian">Sarmatian</a> <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a> entered the peninsula after 409, henceforth weakening the Western Roman Empire's jurisdiction over Hispania. These tribes had crossed the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> in early 407 and ravaged <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a>. The Suebi established a kingdom in north-western Iberia whereas the Vandals established themselves in the south of the peninsula by 420 before crossing over to North Africa in 429. As the western empire disintegrated, the social and economic base became greatly simplified: but even in modified form, the successor regimes maintained many of the institutions and laws of the late empire, including Christianity and assimilation to the evolving Roman culture.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Corona_de_(29049230050).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="1439" decoding="async" height="292" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Corona_de_%2829049230050%29.jpg/140px-Corona_de_%2829049230050%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Corona_de_%2829049230050%29.jpg/210px-Corona_de_%2829049230050%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Corona_de_%2829049230050%29.jpg/280px-Corona_de_%2829049230050%29.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Corona_de_(29049230050).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Votive_crown" title="Votive crown">Votive crown</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reccesuinth" title="Reccesuinth">Reccesuinth</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Treasure_of_Guarrazar" title="Treasure of Guarrazar">Treasure of Guarrazar</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine" title="Byzantine">Byzantines</a> established an occidental province, <a href="/wiki/Spania" title="Spania">Spania</a>, in the south, with the intention of reviving Roman rule throughout Iberia. Eventually, however, Hispania was reunited under <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigothic rule</a>. These <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a>, or Western Goths, after <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Rome_(410)" title="Sack of Rome (410)">sacking Rome</a> under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Alaric_I" title="Alaric I">Alaric</a> (410), turned towards the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Athaulf" title="Athaulf">Athaulf</a> for their leader, and occupied the northeastern portion. <a href="/wiki/Wallia" title="Wallia">Wallia</a> extended his rule over most of the peninsula, keeping the Suebians shut up in Galicia. <a href="/wiki/Theodoric_I" title="Theodoric I">Theodoric I</a> took part, with the Romans and Franks, in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Catalaunian_Plains" title="Battle of the Catalaunian Plains">Battle of the Catalaunian Plains</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Attila" title="Attila">Attila</a> was routed. <a href="/wiki/Euric" title="Euric">Euric</a> (466), who put an end to the last remnants of Roman power in the peninsula, may be considered the first monarch of Spain, though the Suebians still maintained their independence in Galicia. Euric was also the first king to give written laws to the Visigoths. In the following reigns the Catholic kings of France assumed the role of protectors of the Hispano-Roman Catholics against the Arianism of the Visigoths, and in the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Visigothic_Wars" title="Franco-Visigothic Wars">wars</a> which ensued <a href="/wiki/Alaric_II" title="Alaric II">Alaric II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amalaric" title="Amalaric">Amalaric</a> died.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Athanagild" title="Athanagild">Athanagild</a>, having risen against King <a href="/wiki/Agila_I" title="Agila I">Agila</a>, called in the Byzantines and, in payment for the succour they gave him, ceded to them the maritime places of the southeast (554). <a href="/wiki/Liuvigild" title="Liuvigild">Liuvigild</a> restored the political unity of the peninsula, subduing the Suebians, but the religious divisions of the country, reaching even the royal family, brought on a civil war. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Hermengild" title="St. Hermengild">St. Hermengild</a>, the king's son, putting himself at the head of the Catholics, was defeated and taken prisoner, and suffered martyrdom for rejecting communion with the Arians. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recared" title="Recared">Recared</a>, son of Liuvigild and brother of St. Hermengild, added religious unity to the political unity achieved by his father, accepting the Catholic faith in the <a href="/wiki/Third_Council_of_Toledo" title="Third Council of Toledo">Third Council of Toledo</a> (589). The religious unity established by this council was the basis of that fusion of Goths with Hispano-Romans which produced the Spanish nation. <a href="/wiki/Sisebut" title="Sisebut">Sisebut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suintila" title="Suintila">Suintila</a> completed the expulsion of the Byzantines from Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spain_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-Spain-34">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>Intermarriage between Visigoths and Hispano-Romans was prohibited, though in practice it could not be entirely prevented and was eventually legalised by Liuvigild.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[37]</a></sup> The Spanish-Gothic scholars such as <a href="/wiki/Braulio_of_Zaragoza" title="Braulio of Zaragoza">Braulio of Zaragoza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isidore_of_Seville" title="Isidore of Seville">Isidore of Seville</a> played an important role in keeping the classical <a href="/wiki/Greco-Roman_world" title="Greco-Roman world">Greek and Roman culture</a>. Isidore was one of the most influential clerics and philosophers in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> in Europe, and his theories were also vital to the conversion of the Visigothic Kingdom from an <a href="/wiki/Arianism" title="Arianism">Arian</a> domain to a Catholic one in the <a href="/wiki/Councils_of_Toledo" title="Councils of Toledo">Councils of Toledo</a>. Isidore created the first western <a href="/wiki/Etymologiae" title="Etymologiae">encyclopedia</a> which had a huge impact during the Middle Ages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Muslim_era_and_Reconquista">Muslim era and <i>Reconquista</i></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">Umayyad conquest of Hispania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Al-Andalus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a></div>
<p>From 711 to 718, as part of the expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a>, nearly all of the Iberian Peninsula was conquered by Muslim armies from across the Strait of Gibraltar, resulting in the collapse of the Visigothic Kingdom. Only a small area in the mountainous north of the peninsula stood out of the territory seized during the initial invasion. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Asturias" title="Kingdom of Asturias">Kingdom of Asturias-León</a> consolidated upon this pocket of territory. Other Christian kingdoms such as <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">Navarre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">Aragon</a> in the mountainous north eventually surged upon the consolidation of counties of the Carolingian <i><a href="/wiki/Marca_Hispanica" title="Marca Hispanica">Marca Hispanica</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[39]</a></sup> For several centuries, the fluctuating frontier between the Muslim and Christian controlled areas of the peninsula was along the <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">Ebro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">Douro</a> valleys.
</p><p>Under <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Islamic law</a>, Christians and Jews were given the subordinate status of <a href="/wiki/Dhimmi" title="Dhimmi">dhimmi</a>. This status permitted Christians and Jews to practice their religions as <i><a href="/wiki/People_of_the_Book" title="People of the Book">People of the Book</a></i> but they were required to pay a special tax and had legal and social rights inferior to those of Muslims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>Conversion to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> proceeded at an increasing pace. The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muwallad" title="Muwallad">muladíes</a></i> (Muslims of ethnic Iberian origin) are believed to have formed the majority of the population of Al-Andalus by the end of the 10th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chap2_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-chap2-53">[43]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Muslim society was itself diverse and beset by social tensions. The North-African <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berber_people" title="Berber people">Berber peoples</a>, who had provided the bulk of the invading armies, <a href="/wiki/Berber_Revolt" title="Berber Revolt">clashed with the Arab leadership</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[k]</a></sup> Over time, large Moorish populations became established, especially in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guadalquivir_River" title="Guadalquivir River">Guadalquivir River</a> valley, the coastal plain of <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencia</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ebro_River" title="Ebro River">Ebro River</a> valley and (towards the end of this period) in the mountainous region of <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">Granada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chap2_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-chap2-53">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andalusien_2013_(15460132312).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Andalusien_2013_%2815460132312%29.jpg/220px-Andalusien_2013_%2815460132312%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Andalusien_2013_%2815460132312%29.jpg/330px-Andalusien_2013_%2815460132312%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Andalusien_2013_%2815460132312%29.jpg/440px-Andalusien_2013_%2815460132312%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andalusien_2013_(15460132312).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The interior of the <a href="/wiki/Mosque%E2%80%93Cathedral_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Mosque–Cathedral of Córdoba">Great Mosque of Córdoba</a></div></div></div>
<p>A series of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viking" title="Viking">Viking</a> incursions raided the coasts of the Iberian Peninsula in the 9th and 10th centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[44]</a></sup>
</p><p>Córdoba, the capital of the caliphate since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abd-ar-Rahman_III" title="Abd-ar-Rahman III">Abd-ar-Rahman III</a>, was the largest, richest and most sophisticated city in western Europe. Mediterranean trade and cultural exchange flourished. Muslims imported a rich intellectual tradition from the Middle East and North Africa. Some important philosophers at the time were <a href="/wiki/Averroes" title="Averroes">Averroes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Arabi" title="Ibn Arabi">Ibn Arabi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maimonides" title="Maimonides">Maimonides</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanisation_(cultural)" title="Romanisation (cultural)">Romanised</a> cultures of the Iberian Peninsula interacted with Muslim and Jewish cultures in complex ways, giving the region a distinctive culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chap2_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-chap2-53">[43]</a></sup> Outside the cities, where the vast majority lived, the land ownership system from Roman times remained largely intact as Muslim leaders rarely dispossessed landowners and the introduction of new crops and techniques led to an expansion of agriculture introducing new produces which originally came from Asia or the former territories of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 11th century, the Caliphate of Córdoba collapsed, fracturing into a series of petty kingdoms (<i><a href="/wiki/Taifa" title="Taifa">Taifas</a></i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[46]</a></sup> often subject to the payment of a form of <a href="/wiki/Protection_racket" title="Protection racket">protection money</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Parias" title="Parias">Parias</a></i>) to the Northern Christian kingdoms, which otherwise undertook a southward territorial expansion. The capture of the strategic city of <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">Toledo</a> in 1085 marked a significant shift in the balance of power in favour of the Christian kingdoms.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The arrival from North Africa of the Islamic ruling sects of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almoravids" title="Almoravids">Almoravids</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almohads" title="Almohads">Almohads</a> achieved temporary unity upon the Muslim-ruled territory, with a stricter, less tolerant application of Islam, and partially reversed some Christian territorial gains.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leon1030.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="870" data-file-width="1149" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Leon1030.jpg/220px-Leon1030.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Leon1030.jpg/330px-Leon1030.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Leon1030.jpg/440px-Leon1030.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leon1030.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 1030, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">Kingdom of Navarre</a> controlled the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Count_of_Aragon" title="Count of Aragon">Count of Aragon</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Count_of_Castile" title="Count of Castile">Count of Castile</a>, who later became major kingdoms of its time.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Kingdom of León">Kingdom of León</a> was the strongest Christian kingdom for centuries. In 1188 the first modern parliamentary session<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2022)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> in Europe was held in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_(Spain)" title="León (Spain)">León</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cortes_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Cortes of León">Cortes of León</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Kingdom of Castile</a>, formed from Leonese territory, was its successor as strongest kingdom. The kings and the nobility fought for power and influence in this period. The example of the Roman emperors influenced the political objective of the Crown, while the nobles benefited from <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudalism</a>.
</p><p>Muslim strongholds in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guadalquivir_Valley" title="Guadalquivir Valley">Guadalquivir Valley</a> such as Córdoba (1236) and <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a> (1248) fell to Castile in the 13th century. The <a href="/wiki/County_of_Barcelona" title="County of Barcelona">County of Barcelona</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">Kingdom of Aragon</a> entered in a dynastic union and gained territory and power in the Mediterranean. In 1229 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Majorca" title="Majorca">Majorca</a> was conquered, so was <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a> in 1238. In the 13th and 14th centuries, the North-African <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marinid" title="Marinid">Marinids</a> established some enclaves around the Strait of Gibraltar.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Al-andalus_229.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="557" data-file-width="899" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Al-andalus_229.png/220px-Al-andalus_229.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Al-andalus_229.png/330px-Al-andalus_229.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Al-andalus_229.png/440px-Al-andalus_229.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Al-andalus_229.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Miniature from the 13th-century <i><a href="/wiki/Libro_de_los_Juegos" title="Libro de los Juegos">Libro de los Juegos</a></i> depicting a Jew (left) and a Moor (right) playing chess.</div></div></div>
<p>From the mid 13th century, literature and philosophy started to flourish again in the Christian peninsular kingdoms, based on Roman and Gothic traditions. An important philosopher from this time is <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Llull" title="Ramon Llull">Ramon Llull</a>. <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Cresques" title="Abraham Cresques">Abraham Cresques</a> was a prominent Jewish cartographer. <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">Roman law</a> and its institutions were the model for the legislators. The king <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_X_of_Castile" title="Alfonso X of Castile">Alfonso X of Castile</a> focused on strengthening this Roman and Gothic past, and also on linking the Iberian Christian kingdoms with the rest of medieval European <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a>. Alfonso worked for being elected emperor of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> and published the <a href="/wiki/Siete_Partidas" title="Siete Partidas">Siete Partidas</a> code. The <a href="/wiki/Toledo_School_of_Translators" title="Toledo School of Translators">Toledo School of Translators</a> is the name that commonly describes the group of scholars who worked together in the city of Toledo during the 12th and 13th centuries, to translate many of the philosophical and scientific works from <a href="/wiki/Classical_Arabic" title="Classical Arabic">Classical Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Biblical_Hebrew" title="Biblical Hebrew">Ancient Hebrew</a>.
</p><p>The 13th century also witnessed the Crown of Aragon, centred in Spain's north east, expand its reach across islands in the Mediterranean, to <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and Naples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[47]</a></sup> Around this time the universities of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Palencia" title="University of Palencia">Palencia</a> (1212/1263) and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Salamanca" title="University of Salamanca">Salamanca</a> (1218/1254) were established. The <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> of 1348 and 1349 devastated Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Catalans and Aragonese offered themselves to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine_Emperor" title="Byzantine Emperor">Byzantine Emperor</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andronicus_II_Palaeologus" title="Andronicus II Palaeologus">Andronicus II Palaeologus</a> to <a href="/wiki/Catalan_campaign_in_Asia_Minor" title="Catalan campaign in Asia Minor">fight the Turks</a>. Having conquered these, they turned their arms against the Byzantines, who treacherously slew their leaders; but for this treachery, the Spaniards, under Bernard of Rocafort and Berenguer of Entenca, exacted the terrible penalty celebrated in history as "The Catalan Vengeance" and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Halmyros" title="Battle of Halmyros">seized</a> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankish_Greece" title="Frankish Greece">Frankish</a> <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Athens" title="Duchy of Athens">Duchy of Athens</a> (1311).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spain_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-Spain-34">[26]</a></sup> The royal line of Aragon became extinct with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_the_Humane" title="Martin the Humane">Martin the Humane</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Compromise_of_Caspe" title="Compromise of Caspe">Compromise of Caspe</a> gave the Crown to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Trast%C3%A1mara" title="House of Trastámara">House of Trastámara</a>, already reigning in Castile.
</p><p>As in the rest of Europe during the Late Middle Ages, <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Spain" title="Antisemitism in Spain">antisemitism</a> greatly increased during the 14th century in the Christian kingdoms. (A key event in that regard was the Black Death, as Jews were accused of poisoning the waters.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[49]</a></sup> There were mass killings in Aragon in the mid-14th century, and 12,000 Jews were killed in Toledo. In 1391, Christian mobs went from town to town throughout Castile and Aragon, killing an estimated 50,000 Jews.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Bundling_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This claim has too many footnotes for reading to be smooth. (April 2022)">excessive citations</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[55]</a></sup> Women and children were sold as slaves to Muslims, and many synagogues were converted into churches. According to <a href="/wiki/Hasdai_Crescas" title="Hasdai Crescas">Hasdai Crescas</a>, about 70 Jewish communities were destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>This period saw a contrast in landowning characteristics between the western and north-western territories in Andalusia, where the nobility and the religious orders succeeded into the creation of large <i>latifundia</i> entitled to them, whereas in the Kingdom of Granada (eastern Andalusia), a Crown-auspiciated distribution of the land to medium and small farmers took place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[57]</a></sup>
</p><p>Upon the conclusion of the <a href="/wiki/Granada_War" title="Granada War">Granada War</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Granada" title="Kingdom of Granada">Nasrid Sultanate of Granada</a> (the remaining Muslim-ruled polity in the Iberian Peninsula after 1246) capitulated in 1492 to the military strength of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">Catholic Monarchs</a>, and it was integrated from then on in the Crown of Castile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_Empire">Spanish Empire</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1303" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png/260px-Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png/390px-Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png/520px-Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a> in 1598, under <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II</a>, King of Spain and Portugal</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1012" data-file-width="2035" decoding="async" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg/220px-La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg/330px-La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg/440px-La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Late 16th-century Seville, the harbor enjoying the exclusive right to trade with the New World.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1469, the crowns of the Christian kingdoms of Castile and Aragon were united by the marriage of their monarchs, Isabella I and Ferdinand II, respectively. 1478 commenced the completion of the conquest of the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>.
In 1492, Jews were forced to choose between conversion to Catholicism or facing expulsion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[59]</a></sup> As a result, as many as 200,000 Jews were <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_Jews_from_Spain" title="Expulsion of Jews from Spain">expelled from Castile and Aragon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[62]</a></sup> This was followed by expulsions in <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Jews_from_Sicily" title="Expulsion of the Jews from Sicily">1493 in Aragonese Sicily</a> and <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Jews_and_Muslims_by_Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Persecution of Jews and Muslims by Manuel I of Portugal">Portugal in 1497</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Granada" title="Treaty of Granada">Treaty of Granada</a> guaranteed religious tolerance towards Muslims,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[63]</a></sup> for a few years before Islam was outlawed in 1502 in Castile and 1527 in Aragon, leading the remaining Muslim population to become nominally Christian <i><a href="/wiki/Morisco" title="Morisco">Moriscos</a></i>. About four decades after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_the_Alpujarras" title="War of the Alpujarras">War of the Alpujarras</a> (1568–1571), a significant proportion of the <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Moriscos" title="Expulsion of the Moriscos"><i>moriscos</i> were expelled</a>, settling primarily in North Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cong_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-cong-75">[64]</a></sup> From 1609 to 1614, over 300,000 Moriscos were sent on ships to North Africa and other locations, and, of this figure, around 50,000 died resisting the <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Moriscos" title="Expulsion of the Moriscos">expulsion</a>, and 60,000 died on the journey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>The year 1492 also marked the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>, during a voyage funded by Isabella. Columbus's first voyage crossed the Atlantic and reached the Caribbean Islands, beginning the European exploration and conquest of the Americas, although Columbus remained convinced that he had reached the <a href="/wiki/Orient" title="Orient">Orient</a>. Large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous Americans</a> died in battle against the Spaniards during the conquest,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[67]</a></sup> while more died from various new Eurasian diseases that travelled more quickly than the Spanish conquerors. The death toll during the initial period of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish conquest</a>, from Columbus's initial landing until the mid 16th century, is estimated as high as 70 million indigenous people out of a population of 80 million, as imported diseases such as smallpox, measles, influenza, and typhus decimated the pre-Columbian population. Disease killed between 50% and 95% of the indigenous population. Some scholars have described the Spanish conquest during this period as the largest <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENaimark201735_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENaimark201735-79">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="495" data-file-width="618" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg/220px-Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg/330px-Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg/440px-Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cortez_%26_La_Malinche.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lienzo_de_Tlaxcala" title="Lienzo de Tlaxcala">Lienzo de Tlaxcala</a> codex showing the 1519 meeting of <i>conquistador</i> <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernán Cortés">Hernán Cortés</a> and his counsellor <a href="/wiki/La_Malinche" title="La Malinche">La Malinche</a> with Aztec emperor <a href="/wiki/Moctezuma_II" title="Moctezuma II">Moctezuma II</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tenochtitlan" title="Tenochtitlan">Tenochtitlan</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The Spanish colonisation of the Americas started with the colonisation of the Caribbean. It was followed by the conquest of powerful pre-Columbian polities in Central Mexico and the Pacific Coast of South America. <a href="/wiki/Miscegenation" title="Miscegenation">Miscegenation</a> was the rule between the native and the Spanish cultures and people. An expedition sponsored by the Spanish crown completed the first voyage around the world in human history, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_Magellan%E2%80%93Elcano_circumnavigation" title="Timeline of the Magellan–Elcano circumnavigation">Magellan-Elcano circumnavigation</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tornaviaje" title="Tornaviaje">tornaviaje</a> or return route from the Philippines to Mexico made possible the <a href="/wiki/Manila_galleon" title="Manila galleon">Manila galleon</a> trading route. The Spanish encountered Islam in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and in order to incorporate the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, Spanish expeditions organised from newly Christianised <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> had <a href="/wiki/Castilian_War" title="Castilian War">invaded</a> the Philippine territories of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Brunei" title="Sultanate of Brunei">Sultanate of Brunei</a>. The Spanish considered the war with the Muslims of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish-Moro_Wars" title="Spanish-Moro Wars">Brunei and the Philippines</a>, a repeat of the <i>Reconquista</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>A centralisation of royal power ensued in the Early Modern Period at the expense of local nobility, and the word <i>España</i>, whose root is the ancient name <i>Hispania</i>, began to be commonly used to designate the whole of the two kingdoms.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (March 2022)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (March 2022)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:Spain#Dubious" title="Talk:Spain">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cong_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-cong-75">[64]</a></sup>
With their wide-ranging political, legal, religious and military reforms, the Hispanic Monarchy emerged as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historical_powers#Spanish_Empire" title="Historical powers">world power</a>.
</p><p>The unification of the crowns of Aragon and Castile by the marriage of their sovereigns laid the basis for modern Spain and the Spanish Empire, although each kingdom of Spain remained a separate country socially, politically, legally, and in currency and language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[71]</a></sup>
</p><p>Two big revolts broke out during the early reign of the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_monarchy" title="Habsburg monarchy">Habsburg emperor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_the_Comuneros" title="Revolt of the Comuneros">Revolt of the Comuneros</a> in the Crown of Castile and <a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_the_Brotherhoods" title="Revolt of the Brotherhoods">Revolt of the Brotherhoods</a> in the Crown of Aragon.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Spain" title="Habsburg Spain">Habsburg Spain</a> was one of the leading world powers throughout the 16th century and most of the 17th century, a position reinforced by trade and wealth from colonial possessions and became the world's leading <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Navy" title="Spanish Navy">maritime power</a>. It reached its apogee during the reigns of the first two Spanish Habsburgs—Charles V/I (1516–1556) and <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II</a> (1556–1598). This period saw the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Wars" title="Italian Wars">Italian Wars</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Schmalkaldic_War" title="Schmalkaldic War">Schmalkaldic War</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_Revolt" title="Dutch Revolt">Dutch Revolt</a>, the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Portuguese_Succession" title="War of the Portuguese Succession">War of the Portuguese Succession</a>, clashes with the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottomans</a>, intervention in the <a href="/wiki/French_Wars_of_Religion" title="French Wars of Religion">French Wars of Religion</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_War_(1585%E2%80%931604)" title="Anglo-Spanish War (1585–1604)">Anglo-Spanish War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[72]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Principales_Rutas_Comerciales_del_Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2700" data-file-width="5400" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Principales_Rutas_Comerciales_del_Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol.jpg/220px-Principales_Rutas_Comerciales_del_Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Principales_Rutas_Comerciales_del_Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol.jpg/330px-Principales_Rutas_Comerciales_del_Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Principales_Rutas_Comerciales_del_Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol.jpg/440px-Principales_Rutas_Comerciales_del_Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Principales_Rutas_Comerciales_del_Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main Trade Routes of the Spanish Empire</div></div></div>
<p>Through exploration and conquest or royal marriage alliances and inheritance, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> expanded across vast areas in the Americas, the Indo-Pacific, Africa as well as the European continent (including holdings in the Italian Peninsula, the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Franche-Comt%C3%A9" title="Franche-Comté">Franche-Comté</a>). The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Magellan%27s_circumnavigation" title="Timeline of Magellan's circumnavigation">first circumnavigation</a> of the world was carried out in 1519–1521. The so-called <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a> featured explorations by sea and by land, the opening-up of new <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade routes</a> across oceans, conquests and the beginnings of European <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a>. <a href="/wiki/Precious_metal" title="Precious metal">Precious metals</a>, spices, luxuries, and previously unknown plants brought to the metropole played a leading part in transforming the European understanding of the globe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[73]</a></sup> The cultural efflorescence witnessed during this period is now referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Golden_Age" title="Spanish Golden Age">Spanish Golden Age</a>. The expansion of the empire caused immense upheaval in the Americas as the collapse of societies and empires and new diseases from Europe devastated American indigenous populations. The rise of <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">humanism</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">Counter-Reformation</a> and new geographical discoveries and conquests raised issues that were addressed by the intellectual movement now known as the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Salamanca" title="School of Salamanca">School of Salamanca</a>, which developed the first modern theories of what are now known as <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a> and human rights. <a href="/wiki/Juan_Luis_Vives" title="Juan Luis Vives">Juan Luis Vives</a> was another prominent humanist during this period.
</p><p>Spain's 16th-century maritime supremacy was demonstrated by the victory over the Ottomans at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">Lepanto</a> in 1571, and then after the setback of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armada" title="Spanish Armada">Spanish Armada</a> in 1588, in a series of victories against <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_War_(1585%E2%80%931604)" title="Anglo-Spanish War (1585–1604)">Anglo-Spanish War of 1585–1604</a>. However, during the middle decades of the 17th century Spain's maritime power went into a long decline with mounting defeats against the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">United Provinces</a> and then England; that by the 1660s it was struggling grimly to defend its overseas possessions from pirates and privateers.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> dragged the kingdom ever more deeply into the mire of religiously charged wars. The result was a country forced into ever-expanding military efforts across Europe and in the Mediterranean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[74]</a></sup> By the middle decades of a war- and <a href="/wiki/Great_Plague_of_Seville" title="Great Plague of Seville">plague</a>-ridden 17th-century Europe, the Spanish Habsburgs had enmeshed the country in continent-wide religious-political conflicts. These conflicts drained it of resources and undermined the economy generally. Spain managed to hold on to most of the scattered Habsburg empire, and help the imperial forces of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> reverse a large part of the advances made by Protestant forces, but it was finally forced to recognise the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">separation of Portugal</a> and the United Provinces, and eventually suffered some serious military reverses to France in the latter stages of the immensely destructive, Europe-wide <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[75]</a></sup> In the latter half of the 17th century, Spain went into a gradual decline, during which it surrendered several small territories to France and England; however, it maintained and enlarged its vast overseas empire, which remained intact until the beginning of the 19th century.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_familia_de_Felipe_V_(Van_Loo).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2161" data-file-width="2717" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg/220px-La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg/330px-La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg/440px-La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_familia_de_Felipe_V_(Van_Loo).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Family_of_Philip_V_(1743)" title="The Family of Philip V (1743)">The family of Philip V</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_in_Spain" title="Enlightenment in Spain">Enlightenment in Spain</a> a new royal family reigned, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">House of Bourbon</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The decline culminated in a controversy over succession to the throne which consumed the first years of the 18th century. The <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> was a wide-ranging international conflict combined with a civil war, and was to cost the kingdom its European possessions and its position as one of the leading powers on the Continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[76]</a></sup>
During this war, a new dynasty originating in France, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">Bourbons</a>, was installed. The Crowns of Castile and Aragon had been long united only by the Monarchy and the common institution of the Inquisition's <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">Holy Office</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[77]</a></sup> A number of reform policies (the so-called <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Reforms" title="Bourbon Reforms">Bourbon Reforms</a>) were pursued by the Monarchy with the overarching goal of centralized authority and administrative uniformity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[78]</a></sup> They included the abolishment of many of the old regional privileges and laws,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[79]</a></sup> as well as the customs barrier between the Crowns of Aragon and Castile in 1717, followed by the introduction of new property taxes in the Aragonese kingdoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[80]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 18th century saw a gradual recovery and an increase in prosperity through much of the empire. The predominant economic policy was an interventionist one, and the State also pursued policies aiming towards infrastructure development as well as the abolition of internal customs and the reduction of export tariffs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[81]</a></sup> Projects of agricultural colonisation with new settlements took place in the south of Mainland Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartínez_Shaw201614,_23_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartínez_Shaw201614,_23-93">[82]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_in_Spain" title="Enlightenment in Spain">Enlightenment</a> ideas began to gain ground among some of the kingdom's elite and monarchy.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liberalism_and_nation_state">Liberalism and nation state</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid-19th-century_Spain" title="Mid-19th-century Spain">Mid-19th-century Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_in_Spain" title="Anarchism in Spain">Anarchism in Spain</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Second_Republic" title="Spanish Second Republic">Spanish Second Republic</a></div>
