title="Pedro Sánchez (politician)">Pedro Sánchez</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<ul><li><b>Head of State</b> (King)
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Felipe_VI_of_Spain" title="Felipe VI of Spain">Felipe VI</a>, since 19 June 2014</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Government</b></li></ul>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Spain" title="Government of Spain">Government of Spain</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_government_departments" title="Spanish government departments">Spanish government departments</a></div>
<ul><li><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain" title="Prime Minister of Spain">Prime Minister</a> (head of government) or "President of the Government" (<i>Presidente del Gobierno</i>): <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pedro_S%C3%A1nchez_P%C3%A9rez-Castej%C3%B3n" title="Pedro Sánchez Pérez-Castejón">Pedro Sánchez Pérez-Castejón</a>, elected 1 June 2018.</li>
<li>Deputy prime ministers (designated by the Prime Minister): Currently <a href="/wiki/Nadia_Calvi%C3%B1o" title="Nadia Calviño">Nadia Calviño Santamaría</a> (1st), <a href="/wiki/Yolanda_D%C3%ADaz" title="Yolanda Díaz">Yolanda Díaz Pérez</a> (2nd), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teresa_Ribera_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Teresa Ribera Rodríguez">Teresa Ribera Rodríguez</a> (3rd).</li>
<li>Ministers (designated by the Prime Minister): <a href="/wiki/Second_government_of_Pedro_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Second government of Pedro Sánchez">Second government of Pedro Sánchez</a>.</li></ul></li></ul>
<p>The Prime Minister, deputy prime ministers and the rest of ministers convene at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Spain" title="Council of Ministers of Spain">Council of Ministers</a>.
</p><p>Spain is organisationally structured as a so-called <i>Estado de las Autonomías</i> ("State of Autonomies"); it is one of the most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decentralised" title="Decentralised">decentralised</a> countries in Europe, along with Switzerland, Germany and Belgium;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[132]</a></sup> for example, all autonomous communities have their own elected parliaments, governments, <a href="/wiki/Public_Administration_of_Spain" title="Public Administration of Spain">public administrations</a>, budgets, and resources. Health and education systems among others are managed by the Spanish communities, and in addition, the Basque Country and Navarre also manage their own public finances based on <a href="/wiki/Fuero" title="Fuero">foral</a> provisions. In Catalonia, the Basque Country, Navarre and the Canary Islands, a full-fledged autonomous police corps replaces some of the State police functions (see <i><a href="/wiki/Mossos_d%27Esquadra" title="Mossos d'Esquadra">Mossos d'Esquadra</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ertzaintza" title="Ertzaintza">Ertzaintza</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Polic%C3%ADa_Foral" title="Policía Foral">Policía Foral</a>/Foruzaingoa</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Polic%C3%ADa_Canaria" title="Policía Canaria">Policía Canaria</a></i>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Spain" title="Foreign relations of Spain">Foreign relations of Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palau_Reial_Pedralbes_(Barcelona).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2343" data-file-width="4867" decoding="async" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Palau_Reial_Pedralbes_%28Barcelona%29.JPG/220px-Palau_Reial_Pedralbes_%28Barcelona%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Palau_Reial_Pedralbes_%28Barcelona%29.JPG/330px-Palau_Reial_Pedralbes_%28Barcelona%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Palau_Reial_Pedralbes_%28Barcelona%29.JPG/440px-Palau_Reial_Pedralbes_%28Barcelona%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palau_Reial_Pedralbes_(Barcelona).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Palau_Reial_de_Pedralbes" title="Palau Reial de Pedralbes">Palau Reial de Pedralbes</a> in Barcelona, headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Union_for_the_Mediterranean" title="Union for the Mediterranean">Union for the Mediterranean</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>After the return of democracy following the death of <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Franco</a> in 1975, Spain's <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign policy</a> priorities were to break out of the diplomatic isolation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spain_under_Franco" title="Spain under Franco">Franco years</a> and expand <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diplomatic_relations" title="Diplomatic relations">diplomatic relations</a>, enter the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Community</a>, and define security relations with the West.
</p><p>As a member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> since 1982, Spain has established itself as a participant in multilateral international security activities. Spain's EU membership represents an important part of its foreign policy. Even on many international issues beyond western Europe, Spain prefers to coordinate its efforts with its EU partners through the European political co-operation mechanisms.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="This information is too vague. (March 2015)">vague</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Spain has maintained its special relations with <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">Hispanic America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. Its policy emphasises the concept of an <a href="/wiki/Ibero-America" title="Ibero-America">Ibero-American</a> community, essentially the renewal of the concept of <i>"<a href="/wiki/Hispanidad" title="Hispanidad">Hispanidad</a>"</i> or <i>"<a href="/wiki/Hispanism" title="Hispanism">Hispanismo</a>"</i>, as it is often referred to in English, which has sought to link the Iberian Peninsula with Hispanic America through language, commerce, history and culture. It is fundamentally "based on shared values and the recovery of democracy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[133]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Territorial disputes</dt></dl>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_Gibraltar" title="Disputed status of Gibraltar">Spain claims Gibraltar</a>, a 6-square-kilometre (2.3 sq mi) <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">Overseas Territory of the United Kingdom</a> in the southernmost part of the Iberian Peninsula. Then a Spanish town, it was conquered by an Anglo-Dutch force in 1704 during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> on behalf of <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor">Archduke Charles</a>, pretender to the Spanish throne.
</p><p>The legal situation concerning Gibraltar was settled in 1713 by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a>, in which Spain ceded the territory in perpetuity to the British Crown<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[134]</a></sup> stating that, should the British abandon this post, it would be offered to Spain first. Since the 1940s Spain has called for the return of Gibraltar. The overwhelming majority of <a href="/wiki/Gibraltarians" title="Gibraltarians">Gibraltarians</a> strongly oppose this, along with any proposal of shared sovereignty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[135]</a></sup> UN resolutions call on the United Kingdom and Spain to reach an agreement over the status of Gibraltar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[137]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_10000m.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3753" data-file-width="5630" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Gibraltar_10000m.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_10000m.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Gibraltar_10000m.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_10000m.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Gibraltar_10000m.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_10000m.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_10000m.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view showing the <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar" title="Rock of Gibraltar">Rock of Gibraltar</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Gibraltar" title="Isthmus of Gibraltar">isthmus of Gibraltar</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Gibraltar" title="Bay of Gibraltar">Bay of Gibraltar</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The Spanish claim makes a distinction between the <a href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_the_isthmus_between_Gibraltar_and_Spain" title="Disputed status of the isthmus between Gibraltar and Spain">isthmus</a> that connects the Rock to the Spanish mainland on the one hand, and the Rock and city of Gibraltar on the other. While the Rock and city were ceded by the Treaty of Utrecht, Spain asserts that the "occupation of the isthmus is illegal and against the principles of <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">International Law</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[138]</a></sup> The United Kingdom relies on <i>de facto</i> arguments of possession by <a href="/wiki/Prescription_(sovereignty_transfer)" title="Prescription (sovereignty transfer)">prescription</a> in relation to the isthmus,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[139]</a></sup> as there has been "continuous possession [of the isthmus] over a long period".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p>Another dispute surrounds the <a href="/wiki/Savage_Islands" title="Savage Islands">Savage Islands</a>, which Spain acknowledges to be part of <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>. However, Spain claims that they are rocks rather than islands, and therefore Spain does not accept the Portuguese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" title="Exclusive Economic Zone">Exclusive Economic Zone</a> (200 nautical miles) generated by the islands, while acknowledging the <i>Selvagens</i> as possessing <a href="/wiki/Territorial_waters" title="Territorial waters">territorial waters</a> (12 nautical miles). On 5 July 2013, Spain sent a letter to the UN expressing these views.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[142]</a></sup>
</p><p>Spain claims sovereignty over the <a href="/wiki/Perejil_Island" title="Perejil Island">Perejil Island</a>, a small, uninhabited rocky <a href="/wiki/Islet" title="Islet">islet</a> located in the South shore of the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>. The island lies 250 metres (820 ft) just off the coast of Morocco, 8 kilometres (5.0 mi) from <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and 13.5 kilometres (8.4 mi) from mainland Spain. Its sovereignty is disputed between Spain and Morocco. It was the subject of an armed incident between the two countries in 2002. The incident ended when both countries agreed to return to the status quo ante which existed prior to the Moroccan occupation of the island. The islet is now deserted and without any sign of sovereignty.
</p><p>Besides the Perejil Island, the Spanish-held territories claimed by other countries are two: Morocco claims the Spanish cities of Ceuta and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Plazas_de_soberan%C3%ADa" title="Plazas de soberanía">plazas de soberanía</a></i> islets off the northern coast of Africa. Portugal does not recognise Spain's sovereignty over the territory of <a href="/wiki/Olivenza" title="Olivenza">Olivenza</a> which was annexed by Spain in 1801 after the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Oranges" title="War of the Oranges">War of the Oranges</a>. The Portuguese stance is that the territory is <i>de iure</i> Portuguese territory and <i>de facto</i> Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[143]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armed_Forces" title="Spanish Armed Forces">Spanish Armed Forces</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:F-102_Almirante_Juan_de_Borbon_CSSQT.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/F-102_Almirante_Juan_de_Borbon_CSSQT.jpg/220px-F-102_Almirante_Juan_de_Borbon_CSSQT.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/F-102_Almirante_Juan_de_Borbon_CSSQT.jpg/330px-F-102_Almirante_Juan_de_Borbon_CSSQT.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/F-102_Almirante_Juan_de_Borbon_CSSQT.jpg/440px-F-102_Almirante_Juan_de_Borbon_CSSQT.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:F-102_Almirante_Juan_de_Borbon_CSSQT.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Spanish_frigate_Almirante_Juan_de_Borb%C3%B3n" title="Spanish frigate Almirante Juan de Borbón">Almirante Juan de Borbón (F-102)</a>, a Spanish navy's <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_de_Baz%C3%A1n-class_frigate" title="Álvaro de Bazán-class frigate">F100 class</a> frigate incorporating the <a href="/wiki/Aegis_Combat_System" title="Aegis Combat System">Aegis Combat System</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The armed forces of Spain are known as the Spanish Armed Forces (<i>Fuerzas Armadas Españolas</i>). Their <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> is the King of Spain, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Felipe_VI_of_Spain" title="Felipe VI of Spain">Felipe VI</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpanish_Constitution1978Article_62_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpanish_Constitution1978Article_62-155">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>The next military authorities in line are the Prime Minister and the Minister of Defence. The fourth military authority of the State is the <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_Defence_Staff_(Spain)" title="Chief of the Defence Staff (Spain)">Chief of the Defence Staff</a> (JEMAD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[145]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Defence_Staff_(Spain)" title="Defence Staff (Spain)">Defence Staff</a> (<i>Estado Mayor de la Defensa</i>) assists the JEMAD as auxiliary body.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armed_Forces" title="Spanish Armed Forces">Spanish Armed Forces</a> are divided into three branches:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpanish_Constitution1978Article_8_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpanish_Constitution1978Article_8-157">[146]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Spanish_Army" title="Spanish Army">Army (<i>Ejército de Tierra</i>)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spanish_Navy" title="Spanish Navy">Navy (<i>Armada</i>)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spanish_Air_and_Space_Force" title="Spanish Air and Space Force">Air and Space Force (<i>Ejército del Aire y del Espacio</i>)</a></li></ul>
<p>Military conscription was suppressed in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[147]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Spain" title="Human rights in Spain">Human rights in Spain</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Spain" title="LGBT rights in Spain">LGBT rights in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drag-Ybridex-2017-WorldPride-Madrid-Atocha-min_(35794067144).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5000" data-file-width="5000" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Drag-Ybridex-2017-WorldPride-Madrid-Atocha-min_%2835794067144%29.jpg/220px-Drag-Ybridex-2017-WorldPride-Madrid-Atocha-min_%2835794067144%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Drag-Ybridex-2017-WorldPride-Madrid-Atocha-min_%2835794067144%29.jpg/330px-Drag-Ybridex-2017-WorldPride-Madrid-Atocha-min_%2835794067144%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Drag-Ybridex-2017-WorldPride-Madrid-Atocha-min_%2835794067144%29.jpg/440px-Drag-Ybridex-2017-WorldPride-Madrid-Atocha-min_%2835794067144%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Drag-Ybridex-2017-WorldPride-Madrid-Atocha-min_(35794067144).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/WorldPride" title="WorldPride">WorldPride</a> Madrid 2017. A summit on LGBTI human rights took place at the same time as World Pride celebrations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[148]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">Spanish Constitution of 1978</a> "protect all Spaniards and all the peoples of Spain in the exercise of human rights, their cultures and traditions, languages and institutions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpanish_Constitution1978preamble_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpanish_Constitution1978preamble-160">[149]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> (AI), government investigations of alleged police abuses are often lengthy and punishments were light.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[150]</a></sup> Violence against women was a problem, which the Government took steps to address.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[152]</a></sup>
</p><p>Spain provides one of the highest degrees of liberty in the world for its <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> community. Among the countries studied by <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> in 2013, Spain is rated first in acceptance of homosexuality, with 88% of those surveyed saying that homosexuality should be accepted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[153]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Political_divisions_of_Spain" title="Political divisions of Spain">Political divisions of Spain</a></div>
<p>The Spanish State is divided into 17 autonomous communities and 2 autonomous cities, both groups being the highest or first-order administrative division in the country. Autonomous communities are divided into provinces, of which there are 50 in total, and in turn, provinces are divided into municipalities. In Catalonia, two additional divisions exist, the <i>comarques</i> (sing. <i>comarca</i>) and the <i>vegueries</i> (sing. <i>vegueria</i>) both of which have administrative powers; <i>comarques</i> being aggregations of municipalities, and the <i>vegueries</i> being aggregations of <i>comarques</i>. The concept of a <i>comarca</i> exists in all autonomous communities, however, unlike Catalonia, these are merely historical or geographical subdivisions.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Autonomous_communities">Autonomous communities</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">Autonomous communities of Spain</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Nationalities_and_regions_of_Spain" title="Nationalities and regions of Spain">Nationalities and regions of Spain</a></div>
<div class="floatright noresize" role="img" style="width: 410px; line-height: 1; text-align: center; background-color: #ffffff; position: relative;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Autonomous_communities_of_Spain_no_names.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="643" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="377" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain_no_names.svg/410px-Autonomous_communities_of_Spain_no_names.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain_no_names.svg/615px-Autonomous_communities_of_Spain_no_names.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain_no_names.svg/820px-Autonomous_communities_of_Spain_no_names.svg.png 2x" width="410"/></a>

<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:238px; top:75px"><a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragon</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:296px; top:61px"><a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:250px; top:150px"><a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencian<br/>Community</a></div>

<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:104px; top:60px"><a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">Castile<br/>and León</a></div>

<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:178px; top:10px"><a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:211px; top:215.6px"><a href="/wiki/Region_of_Murcia" title="Region of Murcia">Region of<br/>Murcia</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:118px; top:228px"><a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:82px; top:312px"><a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:185.2px; top:332px"><a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:274px; top:14px"><i><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><span style="color: #48A3B5;">France</span></a></i></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:322px; top:128px"><a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic<br/>Islands</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:302px; top:288px"><a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary<br/>Islands</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:282px; top:232px"><i><a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea"><span style="color: #48A3B5;">Mediterranean Sea</span></a></i></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:34px; top:290px"><i><a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean"><span style="color: #48A3B5;">Atlantic<br/>Ocean</span></a></i></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:310px; top:40px"><i><a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra"><span style="color: #48A3B5;">Andorra</span></a></i></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:354px; top:352px"><i><a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean"><span style="color: #48A3B5;">Atlantic<br/>Ocean</span></a></i></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:109px; top:296px"><i><a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar"><span style="color: #48A3B5;">Gibraltar (UK)</span></a></i></div>
</div>
<p>Spain's autonomous communities are the first level administrative divisions of the country. They were created after the current constitution came into effect (in 1978) in recognition of the right to self-government of the "<a href="/wiki/Nationalities_and_regions_of_Spain" title="Nationalities and regions of Spain"><i>nationalities</i> and regions of Spain</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpanish_Constitution1978Article_143_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpanish_Constitution1978Article_143-165">[154]</a></sup> The autonomous communities were to comprise adjacent provinces with common historical, cultural, and economic traits. This territorial organisation, based on <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolution</a>, is known in Spain as the "State of Autonomies".
</p><p>The basic institutional law of each autonomous community is the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy" title="Statute of Autonomy">Statute of Autonomy</a>. The Statutes of Autonomy establish the name of the community according to its historical and contemporary identity, the limits of its territories, the name and organisation of the institutions of government and the rights they enjoy according to the constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpanish_Constitution1978Article_147_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpanish_Constitution1978Article_147-166">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>The governments of all autonomous communities must be based on a division of powers and comprise
</p>
<ul><li>a legislative assembly whose members must be elected by <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> according to the system of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> and in which all areas that integrate the territory are fairly represented;</li>
<li>a government council, with executive and administrative functions headed by a president, elected by the Legislative Assembly and nominated by the King of Spain;</li>
<li>a supreme court, under the supreme court of Spain, which heads the judiciary in the autonomous community.</li></ul>
<p>Catalonia, Galicia and the Basque Country, which identified themselves as <i>nationalities</i>, were granted self-government through a rapid process. Andalusia also identified itself as a nationality in its first Statute of Autonomy, even though it followed the longer process stipulated in the constitution for the rest of the country. Progressively, other communities in revisions to their Statutes of Autonomy have also taken that denomination in accordance with their historical and modern identities, such as the Valencian Community,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[156]</a></sup> the Canary Islands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[157]</a></sup> the Balearic Islands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[158]</a></sup> and Aragon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[159]</a></sup>
</p><p>The autonomous communities have wide legislative and executive autonomy, with their own parliaments and  governments. The distribution of powers may be different for every community, as laid out in their Statutes of Autonomy, since devolution was intended to be asymmetrical. Only two communities—the Basque Country and Navarre—have full fiscal autonomy. Beyond fiscal autonomy, the <i>nationalities</i>—Andalusia, the Basque Country, Catalonia, and Galicia—were devolved more powers than the rest of the communities, among them the ability of the regional president to dissolve the parliament and call for elections at any time. In addition, the Basque Country, Catalonia and Navarre have police corps of their own: <a href="/wiki/Ertzaintza" title="Ertzaintza">Ertzaintza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mossos_d%27Esquadra" title="Mossos d'Esquadra">Mossos d'Esquadra</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Polic%C3%ADa_Foral" title="Policía Foral">Policía Foral</a> respectively. Other communities have more limited forces or none at all, like the <i>Policía Autónoma Andaluza</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cartujo_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-cartujo-171">[160]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a> or the <a href="/wiki/BESCAM" title="BESCAM">BESCAM</a> in Madrid.
</p><p>Nonetheless, recent amendments to existing Statutes of Autonomy or the promulgation of new Statutes altogether, have reduced the asymmetry between the powers originally granted to the <i>nationalities</i> and the rest of the regions.
</p><p>Finally, along with the 17 autonomous communities, two autonomous cities are also part of the State of Autonomies and are first-order territorial divisions: <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a>. These are two exclaves located in the northern African coast.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Provinces_and_municipalities">Provinces and municipalities</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_Spain" title="Local government in Spain">Local government in Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Spain" title="Provinces of Spain">Provinces of Spain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Spain" title="Municipalities of Spain">Municipalities of Spain</a></div>
<p>Autonomous communities are divided into <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Spain" title="Provinces of Spain">provinces</a>, which served as their territorial building blocks. In turn, provinces are divided into <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Spain" title="Municipalities of Spain">municipalities</a>. The existence of both the provinces and the municipalities is guaranteed and protected by the constitution, not necessarily by the Statutes of Autonomy themselves. Municipalities are granted autonomy to manage their internal affairs, and provinces are the territorial divisions designed to carry out the activities of the State.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[161]</a></sup>
</p><p>The current provincial division structure is based—with minor changes—on the <a href="/wiki/1833_territorial_division_of_Spain" title="1833 territorial division of Spain">1833 territorial division</a> by <a href="/wiki/Javier_de_Burgos" title="Javier de Burgos">Javier de Burgos</a>, and in all, the Spanish territory is divided into 50 provinces. The communities of Asturias, Cantabria, La Rioja, the Balearic Islands, Madrid, Murcia and Navarre are the only communities that comprise a single province, which is coextensive with the community itself. In these cases, the administrative institutions of the province are replaced by the governmental institutions of the community.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Spain" title="Economy of Spain">Economy of Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="690" data-file-width="645" decoding="async" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/220px-BlueEurozone.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/330px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/440px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spain is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">European Single Market</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spain_Product_Exports_(2019).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="715" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Spain_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/220px-Spain_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Spain_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/330px-Spain_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Spain_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/440px-Spain_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spain_Product_Exports_(2019).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Spain exports, 2019</div></div></div>
<p>Spain's capitalist <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">14th largest</a> worldwide and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_in_Europe_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of sovereign states in Europe by GDP (nominal)">4th largest</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>'s 4th largest.
</p><p>The centre-right government of former prime minister <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="José María Aznar">José María Aznar</a> worked successfully to gain admission to the group of countries launching the euro in 1999. <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_in_Spain" title="Unemployment in Spain">Unemployment</a> stood at 17.1% in June 2017,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[162]</a></sup> below Spain's early 1990s unemployment rate of at over 20%. The <a href="/wiki/Youth_unemployment_in_Spain" title="Youth unemployment in Spain">youth unemployment</a> rate (35% in March 2018) is extremely high compared to EU standards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[163]</a></sup> Perennial weak points of Spain's economy include a large <a href="/wiki/Informal_economy" title="Informal economy">informal economy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[166]</a></sup> and an education system which OECD reports place among the poorest for developed countries, along with the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[167]</a></sup>
</p><p>By the mid-1990s the economy had commenced the growth that had been disrupted by the global recession of the early 1990s. The strong economic growth helped the government to reduce the government debt as a percentage of GDP and Spain's high unemployment rate began to steadily decline. With the government budget in balance and inflation under control Spain was admitted into the Eurozone in 1999.
</p><p>Since the 1990s some Spanish companies have gained multinational status, often expanding their activities in culturally close Latin America. Spain is the second biggest foreign investor there, after the United States. Spanish companies have also expanded into Asia, especially China and India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Economist2009bet_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-Economist2009bet-179">[168]</a></sup> This early global expansion is a competitive advantage over its competitors and European neighbours. The reason for this early expansion is the booming interest towards Spanish language and culture in Asia and Africa and a corporate culture that learned to take risks in unstable markets.
</p><p>Spanish companies invested in fields like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialisation" title="Renewable energy commercialisation">renewable energy commercialisation</a> (<a href="/wiki/Iberdrola" title="Iberdrola">Iberdrola</a> was the world's largest renewable energy operator<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[169]</a></sup>), technology companies like <a href="/wiki/Telef%C3%B3nica" title="Telefónica">Telefónica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abengoa" title="Abengoa">Abengoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mondragon_Corporation" title="Mondragon Corporation">Mondragon Corporation</a> (which is the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Worker_cooperative" title="Worker cooperative">worker-owned cooperative</a>), <a href="/wiki/Movistar" title="Movistar">Movistar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hisdesat" title="Hisdesat">Hisdesat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indra_Sistemas" title="Indra Sistemas">Indra</a>, train manufacturers like <a href="/wiki/Construcciones_y_Auxiliar_de_Ferrocarriles" title="Construcciones y Auxiliar de Ferrocarriles">CAF</a>, <a href="/wiki/Talgo" title="Talgo">Talgo</a>, global corporations such as the textile company <a href="/wiki/Inditex" title="Inditex">Inditex</a>, petroleum companies like <a href="/wiki/Repsol" title="Repsol">Repsol</a> or <a href="/wiki/Cepsa" title="Cepsa">Cepsa</a> and infrastructure, with six of the ten biggest international construction firms specialising in transport being Spanish, like <a href="/wiki/Ferrovial" title="Ferrovial">Ferrovial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acciona" title="Acciona">Acciona</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grupo_ACS" title="Grupo ACS">ACS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obrasc%C3%B3n_Huarte_Lain" title="Obrascón Huarte Lain">OHL</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fomento_de_Construcciones_y_Contratas" title="Fomento de Construcciones y Contratas">FCC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Economist2009big_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-Economist2009big-181">[170]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005 the <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a> survey placed Spain among the top 10 in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[171]</a></sup> In 2013 the same survey (now called the "Where-to-be-born index"), ranked Spain 28th in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a> was awarded with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lee_Kuan_Yew_World_City_Prize" title="Lee Kuan Yew World City Prize">Lee Kuan Yew World City Prize</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[173]</a></sup> and its mayor at the time, <a href="/wiki/I%C3%B1aki_Azkuna" title="Iñaki Azkuna">Iñaki Azkuna</a>, was awarded the <a href="/wiki/World_Mayor" title="World Mayor">World Mayor</a> Prize in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[174]</a></sup> The Basque capital city of <a href="/wiki/Vitoria-Gasteiz" title="Vitoria-Gasteiz">Vitoria-Gasteiz</a> received the <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Capital_Award" title="European Green Capital Award">European Green Capital Award</a> in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[175]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Automotive_industry">Automotive industry</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_Spain" title="Automotive industry in Spain">Automotive industry in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Factor%C3%ADa_de_Renault_en_Valladolid._Junta_de_Castilla_y_Le%C3%B3n._2018.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="731" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Factor%C3%ADa_de_Renault_en_Valladolid._Junta_de_Castilla_y_Le%C3%B3n._2018.jpg/220px-Factor%C3%ADa_de_Renault_en_Valladolid._Junta_de_Castilla_y_Le%C3%B3n._2018.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Factor%C3%ADa_de_Renault_en_Valladolid._Junta_de_Castilla_y_Le%C3%B3n._2018.jpg/330px-Factor%C3%ADa_de_Renault_en_Valladolid._Junta_de_Castilla_y_Le%C3%B3n._2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Factor%C3%ADa_de_Renault_en_Valladolid._Junta_de_Castilla_y_Le%C3%B3n._2018.jpg/440px-Factor%C3%ADa_de_Renault_en_Valladolid._Junta_de_Castilla_y_Le%C3%B3n._2018.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Factor%C3%ADa_de_Renault_en_Valladolid._Junta_de_Castilla_y_Le%C3%B3n._2018.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Renault factory in <a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a></div></div></div>
<p>The automotive industry is one of the largest employers in the country. In 2015 Spain was the 8th largest automobile producer country in the world and the 2nd largest car manufacturer in Europe after Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ-187">[176]</a></sup>
</p><p>By 2016, the automotive industry was generating 8.7 percent of Spain's <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a>, employing about nine percent of the manufacturing industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ_187-1"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ-187">[176]</a></sup> By 2008 the automobile industry was the 2nd most exported industry<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[177]</a></sup> while in 2015 about 80% of the total production was for export.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ_187-2"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ-187">[176]</a></sup>
</p><p>German companies poured €4.8 billion into Spain in 2015, making the country the second-largest destination for German <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> behind only the U.S. The lion's share of that investment—€4 billion—went to the country's auto industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ_187-3"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ-187">[176]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Spain" title="Agriculture in Spain">Agriculture in Spain</a></div>
<p>Crop areas were farmed in two highly diverse manners. Areas relying on non-irrigated cultivation (<i>secano</i>), which made up 85% of the entire crop area, depended solely on rainfall as a source of water. They included the humid regions of the north and the northwest, as well as vast arid zones that had not been irrigated. The much more productive regions devoted to irrigated cultivation (<i>regadío</i>) accounted for 3 million hectares in 1986, and the government hoped that this area would eventually double, as it already had doubled since 1950. Particularly noteworthy was the development in <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Almer%C3%ADa" title="Province of Almería">Almería</a>—one of the most arid and desolate provinces of Spain—of winter crops of various fruits and vegetables for export to Europe.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Olive_orchards_C%C3%B3rdoba.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3200" data-file-width="4800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Olive_orchards_C%C3%B3rdoba.jpg/220px-Olive_orchards_C%C3%B3rdoba.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Olive_orchards_C%C3%B3rdoba.jpg/330px-Olive_orchards_C%C3%B3rdoba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Olive_orchards_C%C3%B3rdoba.jpg/440px-Olive_orchards_C%C3%B3rdoba.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Olive_orchards_C%C3%B3rdoba.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Olive orchards in <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Though only about 17% of Spain's cultivated land was irrigated, it was estimated to be the source of between 40 and 45% of the gross value of crop production and of 50% of the value of agricultural exports. More than half of the irrigated area was planted in <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fruit_tree" title="Fruit tree">fruit trees</a>, and vegetables. Other agricultural products that benefited from irrigation included grapes, cotton, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_beet" title="Sugar beet">sugar beets</a>, potatoes, <a href="/wiki/Legume" title="Legume">legumes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olive_tree" title="Olive tree">olive trees</a>, mangos, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strawberries" title="Strawberries">strawberries</a>, tomatoes, and <a href="/wiki/Fodder" title="Fodder">fodder</a> grasses. Depending on the nature of the crop, it was possible to harvest two successive crops in the same year on about 10% of the country's irrigated land.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citrus_fruit" title="Citrus fruit">Citrus fruits</a>, vegetables, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cereal_grain" title="Cereal grain">cereal grains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olive_oil" title="Olive oil">olive oil</a>, and wine—Spain's traditional agricultural products—continued to be important in the 1980s. In 1983 they represented 12%, 12%, 8%, 6%, and 4%, respectively, of the country's agricultural production. Because of the changed diet of an increasingly affluent population, there was a notable increase in the consumption of livestock, poultry, and <a href="/wiki/Dairy_product" title="Dairy product">dairy products</a>. Meat production for domestic consumption became the single most important agricultural activity, accounting for 30% of all farm-related production in 1983. Increased attention to livestock was the reason that Spain became a net importer of grains. Ideal growing conditions, combined with proximity to important north European markets, made citrus fruits Spain's leading export. Fresh vegetables and fruits produced through intensive irrigation farming also became important export commodities, as did <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunflower_seed_oil" title="Sunflower seed oil">sunflower seed oil</a> that was produced to compete with the more expensive olive oils in oversupply throughout the Mediterranean countries of the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Community</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Spain" title="Tourism in Spain">Tourism in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Benidormskyline.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Benidormskyline.JPG/220px-Benidormskyline.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Benidormskyline.JPG/330px-Benidormskyline.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Benidormskyline.JPG/440px-Benidormskyline.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Benidormskyline.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Benidorm" title="Benidorm">Benidorm</a>, one of Europe's largest coastal tourist destinations</div></div></div>
<p>In 2017, Spain was the second most visited country in the world, recording 82 million tourists which marked the fifth consecutive year of record-beating numbers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[178]</a></sup> The headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_Organization" title="World Tourism Organization">World Tourism Organization</a> are located in Madrid.
</p><p>Spain's geographic location, popular coastlines, diverse landscapes, historical legacy, vibrant culture, and excellent infrastructure has made the country's international tourist industry among the largest in the world. In the last five decades, international tourism in Spain has grown to become the second largest in the world in terms of spending, worth approximately 40 billion Euros or about 5% of GDP in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guru_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-guru-190">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[180]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castile_and_Leon" title="Castile and Leon">Castile and Leon</a> is the Spanish leader in <a href="/wiki/Rural_tourism" title="Rural tourism">rural tourism</a> linked to its environmental and architectural heritage.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Spain" title="Energy in Spain">Energy in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andasol_Solar_Power_Station_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3030" data-file-width="5000" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Andasol_Solar_Power_Station_2.jpg/220px-Andasol_Solar_Power_Station_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Andasol_Solar_Power_Station_2.jpg/330px-Andasol_Solar_Power_Station_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Andasol_Solar_Power_Station_2.jpg/440px-Andasol_Solar_Power_Station_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andasol_Solar_Power_Station_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Solar power plant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andasol" title="Andasol">Andasol</a> was the first parabolic trough power plant in Europe. Because of the high altitude (1,100 m) and the semi-arid climate, the site has exceptionally high annual direct <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insolation" title="Insolation">insolation</a> of 2,200 kWh/m<sup>2</sup> per year.</div></div></div>
<p>In 2010 Spain became the <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Spain" title="Solar power in Spain">solar power</a> world leader when it overtook the United States with a massive power station plant called <a href="/wiki/Alvarado_I" title="Alvarado I">La Florida</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Badajoz" title="Badajoz">Alvarado, Badajoz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[182]</a></sup> Spain is also Europe's main producer of wind energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[184]</a></sup> In 2010 its wind turbines generated 42,976 GWh, which accounted for 16.4% of all electrical energy produced in Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Graber2005_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-Graber2005-198">[187]</a></sup> On 9 November 2010, wind energy reached an instantaneous historic peak covering 53% of mainland electricity demand<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[188]</a></sup> and generating an amount of energy that is equivalent to that of 14 <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[189]</a></sup> Other renewable energies used in Spain are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_power_plant" title="Hydroelectric power plant">hydroelectric</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gasification_of_biomass" title="Gasification of biomass">biomass</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marine_energy" title="Marine energy">marine</a> (2 power plants under construction).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[190]</a></sup>
</p><p>Non-renewable energy sources used in Spain are <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_plant" title="Nuclear power plant">nuclear</a> (8 operative reactors), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_gas_power_plant" title="Natural gas power plant">gas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coal_power_plant" title="Coal power plant">coal</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_power_plant" title="Oil power plant">oil</a>. Fossil fuels together generated 58% of Spain's electricity in 2009, just below the OECD mean of 61%. Nuclear power generated another 19%, and wind and hydro about 12% each.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SverigeE_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-SverigeE-202">[191]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Spain" title="Transport in Spain">Transport in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Port_of_Valencia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="768" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Port_of_Valencia.jpg/220px-Port_of_Valencia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Port_of_Valencia.jpg/330px-Port_of_Valencia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Port_of_Valencia.jpg/440px-Port_of_Valencia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Port_of_Valencia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Valencia" title="Port of Valencia">Port of Valencia</a>, one of the busiest in the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Banana" title="Golden Banana">Golden Banana</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Spanish road system is mainly centralised, with six highways connecting Madrid to the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencia</a>, West <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>, Extremadura and <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>. Additionally, there are highways along the Atlantic (<a href="/wiki/Ferrol,_Spain" title="Ferrol, Spain">Ferrol</a> to <a href="/wiki/Vigo" title="Vigo">Vigo</a>), Cantabrian (<a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a> to <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n" title="San Sebastián">San Sebastián</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> (<a href="/wiki/Girona" title="Girona">Girona</a> to <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a>) coasts. Spain aims to put one million <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric cars</a> on the road by 2014 as part of the government's plan to save energy and boost <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">energy efficiency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[192]</a></sup> The former Minister of Industry <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Gasc%C3%B3n" title="Miguel Sebastián Gascón">Miguel Sebastián</a> said that "the electric vehicle is the future and the engine of an industrial revolution."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[193]</a></sup>
</p><p>Spain has the most extensive high-speed rail network in Europe, and the second-most extensive in the world after China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[195]</a></sup> As of 2019, Spain has a total of over 3,400 km (2,112.66 mi) of high-speed tracks<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[196]</a></sup> linking <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="Málaga">Málaga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, Madrid, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a>, with the trains operated at commercial speeds up to 310 km/h (190 mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[197]</a></sup> On average, the Spanish high-speed train is the fastest one in the world, followed by the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Shinkansen" title="Shinkansen">bullet train</a> and the French <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[198]</a></sup> Regarding punctuality, it is second in the world (98.5% on-time arrival) after the Japanese Shinkansen (99%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[199]</a></sup> Should the aims of the ambitious <a href="/wiki/AVE" title="AVE">AVE</a> programme (Spanish high speed trains) be met, by 2020 Spain will have 7,000 km (4,300 mi) of high-speed trains linking almost all provincial cities to Madrid in less than three hours and Barcelona within four hours.
</p><p>There are 47 public airports in Spain. The busiest one is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madrid_Airport" title="Madrid Airport">airport of Madrid</a> (Barajas), with 50 million passengers in 2011, being the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">world's 15th busiest airport</a>, as well as the European Union's fourth busiest. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barcelona_Airport" title="Barcelona Airport">airport of Barcelona</a> (El Prat) is also important, with 35 million passengers in 2011, being the world's 31st-busiest airport. Other main airports are located in <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca_Airport" title="Palma de Mallorca Airport">Majorca</a> (23 million passengers), <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_Airport" title="Málaga Airport">Málaga</a> (13 million passengers), <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria_Airport" title="Gran Canaria Airport">Las Palmas (Gran Canaria)</a> (11 million passengers), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alicante_Airport" title="Alicante Airport">Alicante</a> (10 million passengers) and smaller, with the number of passengers between 4 and 10 million, for example <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_South_Airport" title="Tenerife South Airport">Tenerife</a> (two airports), <a href="/wiki/Valencia_Airport" title="Valencia Airport">Valencia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seville_Airport" title="Seville Airport">Seville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bilbao_Airport" title="Bilbao Airport">Bilbao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ibiza_Airport" title="Ibiza Airport">Ibiza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote_Airport" title="Lanzarote Airport">Lanzarote</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura_Airport" title="Fuerteventura Airport">Fuerteventura</a>. Also, more than 30 airports with the number of passengers below 4 million.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Spain" title="Science and technology in Spain">Science and technology in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GranTeCan_Mosaic.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/GranTeCan_Mosaic.jpg/220px-GranTeCan_Mosaic.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/GranTeCan_Mosaic.jpg/330px-GranTeCan_Mosaic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/GranTeCan_Mosaic.jpg/440px-GranTeCan_Mosaic.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GranTeCan_Mosaic.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GranTeCan" title="GranTeCan">GranTeCan</a> reflecting telescope located at <a href="/wiki/Roque_de_los_Muchachos_Observatory" title="Roque de los Muchachos Observatory">Roque de los Muchachos Observatory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Instituto_de_Astrof%C3%ADsica_de_Canarias" title="Instituto de Astrofísica de Canarias">Instituto de Astrofísica de Canarias</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consejo_Superior_de_Investigaciones_Cient%C3%ADficas" title="Consejo Superior de Investigaciones Científicas">Consejo Superior de Investigaciones Científicas</a> (CSIC) is the leading public agency dedicated to scientific research in the country. It ranked as the 5th top governmental scientific institution worldwide (and 32nd overall) in the 2018 SCImago Institutions Rankings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[200]</a></sup> Spain was ranked 30th in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index" title="Global Innovation Index">Global Innovation Index</a> in 2021, down from 29th in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[201]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[204]</a></sup>
</p><p>Higher education institutions (administered at the regional, NUTS2 level) perform about a 60% of the basic research in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[205]</a></sup> Likewise, the contribution of the private sector to R&amp;D expenditures is much lower than in other EU and OECD countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[206]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Mobile_World_Congress" title="Mobile World Congress">Mobile World Congress</a> has taken place in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Spain" title="Demographics of Spain">Demographics of Spain</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Spanish_autonomous_communities_by_population" title="List of Spanish autonomous communities by population">List of Spanish autonomous communities by population</a></div>
<p>In 2019, the population of Spain officially reached 47 million people, as recorded by the <i>Padrón municipal</i> (Spain's Municipal Register).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[207]</a></sup> Spain's population density, at 91/km<sup>2</sup> (235/sq mi), is lower than that of most Western European countries and its distribution across the country is very unequal. With the exception of the region surrounding the capital, Madrid, the most populated areas lie around the coast. The population of Spain has risen 2 1/2 times since 1900, when it stood at 18.6 million, principally due to the spectacular demographic boom in the 1960s and early 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[208]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spain_1950-2014_Population_pyramid.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="465" data-file-width="954" decoding="async" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Spain_1950-2014_Population_pyramid.gif/220px-Spain_1950-2014_Population_pyramid.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Spain_1950-2014_Population_pyramid.gif/330px-Spain_1950-2014_Population_pyramid.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Spain_1950-2014_Population_pyramid.gif/440px-Spain_1950-2014_Population_pyramid.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spain_1950-2014_Population_pyramid.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">Population pyramid</a> of Spain from 1950 to 2014</div></div></div>
<p>In 2017, the average <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> (TFR) across Spain was 1.33 children born per woman,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[209]</a></sup> one of the lowest in the world, below the replacement rate of 2.1, it remains considerably below the high of 5.11 children born per woman in 1865.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[210]</a></sup> Spain subsequently has one of the oldest populations in the world, with the average age of 43.1 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[211]</a></sup>
</p><p>Native <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spaniards</a> make up 88% of the total population of Spain. After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_territories_by_fertility_rate" title="List of countries and territories by fertility rate">birth rate</a> plunged in the 1980s and Spain's population growth rate dropped, the population again trended upward initially upon the return of many Spaniards who had emigrated to other European countries during the 1970s, and more recently, fuelled by large numbers of immigrants who make up 12% of the population. The immigrants originate mainly in Latin America (39%), North Africa (16%), Eastern Europe (15%), and <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a> (4%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[212]</a></sup> In 2005, Spain instituted a three-month amnesty programme through which certain hitherto undocumented aliens were granted legal residency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, Spain granted citizenship to 84,170 persons, mostly to people from Ecuador, Colombia and Morocco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[214]</a></sup> Many foreign residents in Spain also come from other Western and Central European countries. These are mostly British, French, German, Dutch, and Norwegian. They reside primarily on the Mediterranean coast and the Balearic islands, where many are retired or <a href="/wiki/Remote_work" title="Remote work">remote workers</a>.
</p><p>Substantial populations descended from Spanish colonists and immigrants exist in other parts of the world, most notably in Latin America. Beginning in the late 15th century, large numbers of Iberian colonists settled in what became Latin America and at present most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Latin_American" title="White Latin American">white Latin Americans</a> (who make up about one-third of Latin America's population) are of Spanish or Portuguese origin. Around 240,000 Spaniards emigrated in the 16th century, mostly to <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[215]</a></sup> Another 450,000 left in the 17th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[216]</a></sup> The estimate between 1492 and 1832 is 1.86 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[217]</a></sup> Between 1846 and 1932 it is estimated that nearly 5 million Spaniards emigrated to the Americas, especially to <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[218]</a></sup> Approximately two million Spaniards migrated to other Western European countries between 1960 and 1975. During the same period perhaps 300,000 went to Latin America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[219]</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Peoples">Peoples</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spaniards</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_and_regional_identity_in_Spain" title="National and regional identity in Spain">National and regional identity in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:191026_60278_dc_(48979567256).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3888" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/191026_60278_dc_%2848979567256%29.jpg/220px-191026_60278_dc_%2848979567256%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/191026_60278_dc_%2848979567256%29.jpg/330px-191026_60278_dc_%2848979567256%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/191026_60278_dc_%2848979567256%29.jpg/440px-191026_60278_dc_%2848979567256%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:191026_60278_dc_(48979567256).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Catalans" title="Catalans">Catalan people</a> in Barcelona in 2019</div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">Spanish Constitution of 1978</a>, in its second article, generically recognises contemporary entities—'<i><a href="/wiki/Nationalities_and_regions_of_Spain" title="Nationalities and regions of Spain">nationalities</a></i> and regions'—<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nationalities_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nationalities-236">[l]</a></sup> within the context of the Spanish nation.
</p><p>Spain has been described as a <i>de facto</i> <a href="/wiki/Plurinationalism" title="Plurinationalism">plurinational state</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[225]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[226]</a></sup> The identity of Spain rather accrues of an overlap of different territorial and ethnolinguistic identities than of a sole Spanish identity. In some cases some of the territorial identities may conflict with the dominant Spanish culture. Distinct traditional identities within Spain include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basque_people" title="Basque people">Basques</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catalan_people" title="Catalan people">Catalans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galician_people" title="Galician people">Galicians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andalusians" title="Andalusians">Andalusians</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valencian_people" title="Valencian people">Valencians</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (June 2021)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[227]</a></sup> although to some extent all of the 17 autonomous communities may claim a distinct local identity.
</p><p>It is this last feature of "shared identity" between the more local level or autonomous community and the Spanish level which makes the identity question in Spain complex and far from univocal.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minority_groups">Minority groups</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mayer_recibe_la_bandera_gitana_en_el_D%C3%ADa_de_las_gitanas_y_gitanos_de_Madrid_03.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Mayer_recibe_la_bandera_gitana_en_el_D%C3%ADa_de_las_gitanas_y_gitanos_de_Madrid_03.jpg/220px-Mayer_recibe_la_bandera_gitana_en_el_D%C3%ADa_de_las_gitanas_y_gitanos_de_Madrid_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Mayer_recibe_la_bandera_gitana_en_el_D%C3%ADa_de_las_gitanas_y_gitanos_de_Madrid_03.jpg/330px-Mayer_recibe_la_bandera_gitana_en_el_D%C3%ADa_de_las_gitanas_y_gitanos_de_Madrid_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Mayer_recibe_la_bandera_gitana_en_el_D%C3%ADa_de_las_gitanas_y_gitanos_de_Madrid_03.jpg/440px-Mayer_recibe_la_bandera_gitana_en_el_D%C3%ADa_de_las_gitanas_y_gitanos_de_Madrid_03.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mayer_recibe_la_bandera_gitana_en_el_D%C3%ADa_de_las_gitanas_y_gitanos_de_Madrid_03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Celebration of the Romani Day on 24 May 2018 in Madrid</div></div></div>
<p>Spain has a number of descendants of populations from former colonies, especially Latin America and North Africa. Smaller numbers of immigrants from several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan" title="Sub-Saharan">Sub-Saharan</a> countries have recently been settling in Spain. There are also sizeable numbers of Asian immigrants, most of whom are of Middle Eastern, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Asian" title="South Asian">South Asian</a> and Chinese origin. The single largest group of immigrants are European; represented by large numbers of Romanians, Britons, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>, French and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[228]</a></sup>
</p><p>The arrival of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roma_in_Spain" title="Roma in Spain">gitanos</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani people</a>, began in the 16th century; estimates of the Spanish Roma population range from 750,000 to over one million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diagnostico_Social_de_la_Comunidad_Gitana_en_Espana_–_CIS_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-Diagnostico_Social_de_la_Comunidad_Gitana_en_Espana_–_CIS-241">[229]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[230]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[231]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-immigration_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-immigration-244">[232]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[233]</a></sup> There are also the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merchero" title="Merchero">mercheros</a></i> (also <i>quinquis</i>), a formerly nomadic minority group. Their origin is unclear.
</p><p>Historically, <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardi Jews</a> and Moriscos are the main minority groups originating in Spain and with a contribution to Spanish culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[234]</a></sup> The Spanish government is offering Spanish nationality to Sephardi Jews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[235]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Spain" title="Immigration to Spain">Immigration to Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Distribuci%C3%B3n_de_la_poblaci%C3%B3n_extranjera_en_Espa%C3%B1a_(2005).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="539" data-file-width="813" decoding="async" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Distribuci%C3%B3n_de_la_poblaci%C3%B3n_extranjera_en_Espa%C3%B1a_%282005%29.png/300px-Distribuci%C3%B3n_de_la_poblaci%C3%B3n_extranjera_en_Espa%C3%B1a_%282005%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Distribuci%C3%B3n_de_la_poblaci%C3%B3n_extranjera_en_Espa%C3%B1a_%282005%29.png/450px-Distribuci%C3%B3n_de_la_poblaci%C3%B3n_extranjera_en_Espa%C3%B1a_%282005%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Distribuci%C3%B3n_de_la_poblaci%C3%B3n_extranjera_en_Espa%C3%B1a_%282005%29.png/600px-Distribuci%C3%B3n_de_la_poblaci%C3%B3n_extranjera_en_Espa%C3%B1a_%282005%29.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Distribuci%C3%B3n_de_la_poblaci%C3%B3n_extranjera_en_Espa%C3%B1a_(2005).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Distribution of the foreign population in Spain in 2005 by percentage</div></div></div>
