Each municipality is allowed to declare a maximum of 14 public holidays per year; up to nine of these are chosen by the national government and at least two are chosen locally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[314]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/National_Day_of_Spain" title="National Day of Spain">Spain's National Day</a> (<i>Fiesta Nacional de España</i>) is celebrated on 12 October, the anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_North_America" title="Exploration of North America">Discovery of America</a> and commemorate <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_the_Pillar" title="Our Lady of the Pillar">Our Lady of the Pillar</a> feast, patroness of <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragon</a> and throughout Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327"><a href="#cite_note-327">[315]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[316]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are many festivals and festivities in Spain. Some of them are known worldwide, and millions of tourists from all over the world go to Spain annually to experience one of these festivals. One of the most famous is <a href="/wiki/Festival_of_San_Ferm%C3%ADn" title="Festival of San Fermín">San Fermín</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Pamplona" title="Pamplona">Pamplona</a>. While its most famous event is the <i>encierro</i>, or the <a href="/wiki/Running_of_the_bulls" title="Running of the bulls">running of the bulls</a>, which happens at 8:00 am from 7 to 14 July, the seven days-long celebration involves many other traditional and folkloric events. The events were central to the plot of The Sun Also Rises, by <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Hemingway" title="Ernest Hemingway">Ernest Hemingway</a>, which brought it to the general attention of English-speaking people. As the result, it has become one of the most internationally renowned fiestas in Spain, with over 1,000,000 people attending every year.
</p><p>Other festivals include: <a href="/wiki/La_Tomatina" title="La Tomatina">La Tomatina</a> tomato festival in <a href="/wiki/Bu%C3%B1ol" title="Buñol">Buñol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencia</a>, the carnivals in the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Falles" title="Falles">Falles</a> in <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Week" title="Holy Week">Holy Week</a> in Andalusia and <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">Castile and León</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-es_lang-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-es_lang_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In Spain, some <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Spain" title="Languages of Spain">other languages</a> enjoy co-official status in certain regions in accordance with the latter's <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy" title="Statute of Autonomy">Statutes of Autonomy</a>. In each of these, Spain's conventional long name for international affairs in Spanish laws and the most used (Spanish: <i lang="es">Reino de España</i>, pronounced: <small></small><span class="IPA" lang="es-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[ˈrejno ð(e) esˈpaɲa]</a></span>) is as follows:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>: <i lang="ca">Regne d'Espanya</i>, <small>IPA: </small><span class="IPA" lang="ca-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">[ˈreŋnə ðəsˈpaɲə]</a></span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a>: <i lang="eu">Espainiako Erresuma</i>, <small>IPA: </small><span class="IPA" lang="eu-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Basque" title="Help:IPA/Basque">[es̺paɲiako eres̺uma]</a></span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a>: <i lang="gl">Reino de España</i>, <small>IPA: </small><span class="IPA" lang="gl-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Galician" title="Help:IPA/Galician">[ˈrejnʊ ð(ɪ) esˈpaɲɐ]</a></span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a>: <i lang="oc">Reiaume d'Espanha</i>, <small>IPA: </small><span class="IPA" lang="oc-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Occitan" title="Help:IPA/Occitan">[reˈjawme ðesˈpaɲɔ]</a></span></li></ul>
</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-c-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-c_4-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The official language of the State is established in the Section 3 of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">Spanish Constitution of 1978</a> to be Castilian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[2]</a></sup> In some <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous communities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan/Valencian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a> (locally known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aranese_language" title="Aranese language">Aranese</a>) are co-official languages. <a href="/wiki/Aragonese_language" title="Aragonese language">Aragonese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">Asturian</a> have some degree of government recognition at the regional level.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) since 1993.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">On 1 January 2020, the Spanish population was 47.330 million, an increase of 392,921. In the same period, the number of citizens with Spanish citizenship reached 42,094,606. The number of foreigners (i.e. immigrants, ex-pats and refugees, without including foreign born nationals with Spanish citizenship) permanently living in Spain was estimated to be at 5,235,375 (11.06%) in 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cp_2020_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-cp_2020-11">[8]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_peseta" title="Spanish peseta">Peseta</a> before 2002.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-e-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-e_17-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/.eu" title=".eu">.eu</a> domain is also used, as it is shared with other <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> member states. Also, the <a href="/wiki/.cat" title=".cat">.cat</a> domain is used in <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/.gal" title=".gal">.gal</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galiza" title="Galiza">Galicia</a> and <a href="/wiki/.eus" title=".eus">.eus</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque-Country</a> autonomous regions.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-nation_name-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-nation_name_18-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Spanish Constitution does not contain any one official name for Spain. Instead, the terms <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">España</i></span> (Spain), <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Estado español</i></span> (Spanish State) and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Nación española</i></span> (Spanish Nation) are used throughout the document, sometimes interchangeably. In 1984, the Spanish Ministry of Foreign Affairs established that the denominations <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">España</i></span> (Spain) and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Reino de España</i></span> (Kingdom of Spain) are equally valid to designate Spain in international treaties. The latter term is widely used by the government in national and international affairs of all kinds, including foreign treaties as well as national official documents, and is therefore recognised as the conventional name by many international organisations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nj_329-0"><a href="#cite_note-nj-329">[317]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">list of transcontinental countries</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latifundia" title="Latifundia">latifundia</a></i> (sing., <i>latifundium</i>), large estates controlled by the aristocracy, were superimposed on the existing Iberian landholding system.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-45">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The poets <a href="/wiki/Martial" title="Martial">Martial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quintilian" title="Quintilian">Quintilian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lucan" title="Lucan">Lucan</a> were also born in Hispania.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Berbers soon gave up attempting to settle the harsh lands in the north of the <a href="/wiki/Meseta_Central" title="Meseta Central">Meseta Central</a> (Inner Plateau) handed to them by the Arab rulers.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Nationalities-236"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Nationalities_236-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The term 'nationality' (Spanish: <i lang="es">nacionalidad</i>) was chosen carefully in order to avoid the more politically charged term 'nation'.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

</div></td></tr></tbody></table><div></div></td></tr><tr><td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3"><div><div class="hlist hlist-separated"><ul><li><sup>1</sup> Spans the conventional boundary between Europe and another continent.</li><li><sup>2</sup> Considered European for cultural, political and historical reasons but is geographically in Western Asia.</li><li><sup>3</sup> <a href="/wiki/Island#Oceanic_islands" title="Island">Oceanic islands</a> within the vicinity of Europe are usually grouped with the continent even though they are not situated on its continental shelf.</li></ul></div>
